[2] The copyright holder, Uchibori Akira (hereinafter referred to as "Party A"), and EPSILON PROJECT INC. (Epsilon Research and Development Co., Ltd., hereinafter referred to as "Party B"), have entered into the following agreement regarding the use of the copyright for the work "Brain Damage" by Party A.
[3] Party A agrees that Party B may use the work for the game device "KLEIN-2 (tentative name)" as the original software within five years from the signing of this agreement in various promotional materials for the game device and engage in profit-making sales at amusement facilities nationwide.
[4] Party A agrees that Party B may use the work as specified in this agreement to create and use various promotional materials for the game software and device.
[5] Party B shall pay Party A JPY 2 million (including tax) within one month from the signing of this agreement as the copyright use fee for the first two items.
[6] During the five-year period from the signing of this agreement, Party A shall not create or authorize a third party other than Party B to create secondary works based on the work for games, movies, television programs, radio programs, and publications.
[7] In case of any breach of this agreement by either Party A or Party B, the other party may immediately terminate this agreement and claim damages if any loss is incurred.
[8] If Party B wishes to continue using the work after the expiration of the initial term, it must first obtain Party A's written consent, and the copyright use fee shall be determined by Party A and Party B through separate negotiations.
[9] Any matters not specified in this agreement shall be resolved through negotiation between Party A and Party B in good faith.
[10] This agreement shall be in two copies, with one copy each retained by Party A and Party B after signing.

[18] This is the contract I signed with Ypsilon Company. Although I'm not sure how effective it is, I still decided to put it on the first page of my notebook.
[19] If someone questions the authenticity of the contract, they can carefully tear it off and take it to a scientific examination, where they should be able to find a lot of evidence.
[20] For example, there is a small, unobtrusive stain about 2.5 centimeters below my signature, which is actually my left index finger's partial fingerprint. Before signing, I accidentally smudged the contract with ink from a pen I used to write a few characters on a blank newspaper, soiling it. When I noticed the stain while preparing to seal the contract, I was going to sign a new one, but the other party said it was fine, so I let it go.
[21] In addition to my fingerprint, the contract can at least identify the fingerprints of two other people. Of course, this is assuming that these fingerprints have not disappeared over time.
[22] The first person's name is Kajiura Takao, the head of the Sales Planning Department at Ipsilon Inc., and he was the one who brought the contract.
[23] "Please sign here, stamp below, and then stack the two contracts together and stamp them with a seal."
[24] He said this while pointing out the places that needed to be filled or stamped, so there are likely to be a lot of his fingerprints on the contract.
[25] The other person is my sister-in-law, Fukuda Yoshihiro. Since the game based on my work is about to be made, it is a great joy for me, so I took the contract to my sister's house to show off. At that time, Fukuda-san was preparing dinner, so she asked Yoshihiro to hold the contract to avoid getting it wet. Therefore, there are no fingerprints of Fukuda-san on the contract.
[26] The evidence found on the contract is not only fingerprints. I have read in books that blood types can also be tested from sweat and saliva. I don't know if Kajiwara Takahiro had the habit of licking his fingers when turning the pages, but if he did, there might be traces of it in one corner of the contract.
[27] In any case, after precise identification, it can be proven that the contract is genuine. Even if those people deny it under the instigation of the person behind the scenes, the contract can prove my relationship with Ipsilon Corporation. The liar is not me, but those who slander me.
[28] I am now in exile.
[29] I am staying in an old, dilapidated building that looks like an abandoned villa in the mountains. The firewood piled up inside is covered with moss, and the bicycle lying at the door is rusted and unusable, indicating that it has been a long time since anyone has lived here. I am sitting in the attic, writing this notebook.
[30] Initially, I took shelter under the balcony to avoid the rain. I parted the weeds, crawled on the wet ground, and saw a cracked concrete wall in front of me. There was a small window about 50 centimeters wide and long on the wall, the wooden frame of which was shaking, and it would fall off with a slight pull. After removing the spider web, I saw three twisted iron pieces, which were probably ventilation fans. After kicking them, the iron fan blades fell into the darkness and made a loud noise. Then, I crawled inside.
[31] It seemed to be a mechanical room, with a small boiler on the concrete floor and rusty iron pipes running along the wall. There was a door opposite it. The floor and walls were damp, and the space was eerily silent. I opened the door and came to a place that looked like an underground storage room. There was a row of wooden shelves along the wall, cluttered with paper boxes that had swollen and deformed due to moisture. I wanted to pull one out to take a look, but a mouse suddenly darted out of the gap between the boxes, startling me and causing me to quickly retract my hand.
[32] The storage room was narrow, and I climbed up the stairs at the end. The left side of the first floor corridor was the kitchen, and the right side was the living room. Straight ahead led to the front door.
[33] Within ten minutes, I had explored the entire house. It was a two-story building with a living room, a Japanese-style room, and a dining room on the first floor, and only two bedrooms on the second floor. There was a ladder next to the deeper bedroom wall, which led to the attic where I am now. It is about four tatami mats in size, but the view outside the window is excellent, with a green hillside extending to the valley and distant mountain ranges in the distance.
[34] However, the most important thing is that I can see the road in front of the house from the window. Whenever someone comes up the mountain, I can see it from a distance. The mountain road leading to the county road flows along the stream to the peak, and occasionally there are villagers driving small pickup trucks up the mountain or hikers walking slowly, but most of the time it is deserted. It is impossible for an uninvited guest to turn into the side road and approach this abandoned house.
[35] I like the environment here, so I returned to the basement, crawled out of the ventilation fan window, and went to the village at the foot of the mountain to buy food and notebooks. Then, I moved tables and chairs to the window in the attic and sat down at the table, flipping through the notebook. As long as I look up, the road in front of the house is visible. If I notice someone approaching, I can hide with the notebook in the basement in less than three minutes.
[36] I have at least enough cash to live for a month, which should be enough to finish writing down the whole story.
[37] So, where should I start writing?
[38] Regardless of the outcome, the only thing I can do now is to record everything that has happened. I don't know how much meaning or value it has, but I don't want to think about the meaning and truth of things anymore. Pursuing it further will only lead me down another dead end.
[39] Now, I am like a giant snake that keeps swallowing its own tail.
[40] In the end, what will be left? A skin and stomach that is turned inside out? Or a form that has completely disappeared, leaving only an unsatisfied consciousness?
[41] Now, I just hope that something will be left behind, even if it's just a small piece of debris.
